# Listener implementation\\n2: \\n3: ## Socket handling\\n4: \\n5: Envoy uses the following procedure for creating sockets and assigning them to workers.\\n6: \\n7: 1. When a listener is created, a socket is pre-created for every worker on the main thread. This\\n8:    allows most errors to be caught early on in the listener creation process (e.g., bad socket\\n9:    option, unable to bind, etc.).\\n10:     * If using reuse_port, a unique socket is created for every worker.\\n11:     * If not using reuse_port, a unique socket is created for worker 0, and then that socket\\n12:       is duplicated for all other workers.\\n13: 2. In the case of a listener update in which the address/socket is to be shared (i.e., a named\\n14:    listener that has configuration settings changed but listens on the same address will share\\n15:    sockets with the draining listener), all sockets are duplicated regardless of whether using\\n16:    reuse_port or not. This keeps the logic equivalent, and also makes sure that when using\\n17: \",\"endLine\":17,\"startLine\":1},{\"content\":\"17:    reuse_port no TCP connections are dropped during the drain process (in the race condition between\\n18:    assigning a queue and closing the listening socket on the old listener).\\n19: 3. In the case of hot restart, all sockets are requested by worker index. If the old process has\\n20:    a match, the socket is duplicated and sent to the new process. Thus, hot restart and a listener\\n21:    update effectively share the same update process. This is so that no connections are dropped\\n22: \",\"endLine\":22,\"startLine\":17},{\"content\":\"22:    when using reuse_port.\\n23: 4. A consequence of every listener having dedicated sockets (whether duplicated or not) is that\\n24:    a listener can close() its sockets when removed without concern for other listeners.\\n25: \\n26: For more information, see `ListenSocketFactoryImpl` and its use within `ListenerImpl` and\\n27: `ListenerManagerImpl`.\\n28: \",\"endLine\":28,\"startLine\":22}],\"file\":\"source/docs/listener.md\",\"repo\":\"github.com/sg-evals/envoy--v1.31.2\",\"type\":\"file\",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/envoy--v1.31.2/-/blob/source/docs/listener.md\"},{\"chunks\":[{\"content\":\"745: \\n746: void ListenerManagerImpl::addListenerToWorker(Worker& worker,\\n747:                                               absl::optional<uint64_t> overridden_listener,\\n748:                                               ListenerImpl& listener,\\n749:                                               ListenerCompletionCallback completion_callback) {\\n750:   if (overridden_listener.has_value()) {\\n751:     ENVOY_LOG(debug, \\\"replacing existing listener {}\\\", overridden_listener.value());\\n752:   }\\n753:   worker.addListener(\\n754:       overridden_listener, listener,\\n755:       [this, completion_callback]() -> void {\\n756:         // The add listener completion runs on the worker thread. # Listener implementation\\n2: \\n3: ## Socket handling\\n4: \\n5: Envoy uses the following procedure for creating sockets and assigning them to workers.\\n6: \\n7: 1. When a listener is created, a socket is pre-created for every worker on the main thread. This\\n8:    allows most errors to be caught early on in the listener creation process (e.g., bad socket\\n9:    option, unable to bind, etc.).\\n10:     * If using reuse_port, a unique socket is created for every worker.\\n11:     * If not using reuse_port, a unique socket is created for worker 0, and then that socket\\n12:       is duplicated for all other workers.\\n13: 2. In the case of a listener update in which the address/socket is to be shared (i.e., a named\\n14:    listener that has configuration settings changed but listens on the same address will share\\n15:    sockets with the draining listener), all sockets are duplicated regardless of whether using\\n16:    reuse_port or not. This keeps the logic equivalent, and also makes sure that when using\\n17: \",\"endLine\":17,\"startLine\":1},{\"content\":\"17:    reuse_port no TCP connections are dropped during the drain process (in the race condition between\\n18:    assigning a queue and closing the listening socket on the old listener).\\n19: 3. In the case of hot restart, all sockets are requested by worker index. If the old process has\\n20:    a match, the socket is duplicated and sent to the new process. Thus, hot restart and a listener\\n21:    update effectively share the same update process. This is so that no connections are dropped\\n22: \",\"endLine\":22,\"startLine\":17},{\"content\":\"22:    when using reuse_port.\\n23: 4. A consequence of every listener having dedicated sockets (whether duplicated or not) is that\\n24:    a listener can close() its sockets when removed without concern for other listeners.\\n25: \\n26: For more information, see `ListenSocketFactoryImpl` and its use within `ListenerImpl` and\\n27: `ListenerManagerImpl`.\\n28: \",\"endLine\":28,\"startLine\":22}],\"file\":\"source/docs/listener.md\",\"repo\":\"github.com/sg-evals/envoy--v1.31.2\",\"type\":\"file\",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/envoy--v1.31.2/-/blob/source/docs/listener.md\"},{\"chunks\":[{\"content\":\"745: \\n746: void ListenerManagerImpl::addListenerToWorker(Worker& worker,\\n747:                                               absl::optional<uint64_t> overridden_listener,\\n748:                                               ListenerImpl& listener,\\n749:                                               ListenerCompletionCallback completion_callback) {\\n750:   if (overridden_listener.has_value()) {\\n751:     ENVOY_LOG(debug, \\\"replacing existing listener {}\\\", overridden_listener.value());\\n752:   }\\n753:   worker.addListener(\\n754:       overridden_listener, listener,\\n755:       [this, completion_callback]() -> void {\\n756:         // The add listener completion runs on the worker thread. # Listener implementation\n2: \n3: ## Socket handling\n4: \n5: Envoy uses the following procedure for creating sockets and assigning them to workers.\n6: \n7: 1. When a listener is created, a socket is pre-created for every worker on the main thread. This\n8:    allows most errors to be caught early on in the listener creation process (e.g., bad socket\n9:    option, unable to bind, etc.).\n10:     * If using reuse_port, a unique socket is created for every worker.\n11:     * If not using reuse_port, a unique socket is created for worker 0, and then that socket\n12:       is duplicated for all other workers.\n13: 2. In the case of a listener update in which the address/socket is to be shared (i.e., a named\n14:    listener that has configuration settings changed but listens on the same address will share\n15:    sockets with the draining listener), all sockets are duplicated regardless of whether using\n16:    reuse_port or not. This keeps the logic equivalent, and also makes sure that when using\n17: ","endLine":17,"startLine":1},{"content":"17:    reuse_port no TCP connections are dropped during the drain process (in the race condition between\n18:    assigning a queue and closing the listening socket on the old listener).\n19: 3. In the case of hot restart, all sockets are requested by worker index. If the old process has\n20:    a match, the socket is duplicated and sent to the new process. Thus, hot restart and a listener\n21:    update effectively share the same update process. This is so that no connections are dropped\n22: ","endLine":22,"startLine":17},{"content":"22:    when using reuse_port.\n23: 4. A consequence of every listener having dedicated sockets (whether duplicated or not) is that\n24:    a listener can close() its sockets when removed without concern for other listeners.\n25: \n26: For more information, see `ListenSocketFactoryImpl` and its use within `ListenerImpl` and\n27: `ListenerManagerImpl`.\n28: ","endLine":28,"startLine":22}],"file":"source/docs/listener.md","repo":"github.com/sg-evals/envoy--v1.31.2","type":"file","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/envoy--v1.31.2/-/blob/source/docs/listener.md"},{"chunks":[{"content":"745: \n746: void ListenerManagerImpl::addListenerToWorker(Worker& worker,\n747:                                               absl::optional<uint64_t> overridden_listener,\n748:                                               ListenerImpl& listener,\n749:                                               ListenerCompletionCallback completion_callback) {\n750:   if (overridden_listener.has_value()) {\n751:     ENVOY_LOG(debug, \"replacing existing listener {}\", overridden_listener.value());\n752:   }\n753:   worker.addListener(\n754:       overridden_listener, listener,\n755:       [this, completion_callback]() -> void {\n756:         // The add listener completion runs on the worker thread. ],\n  \"text\": \"The Envoy listener manager is implemented across multiple C++ files in the envoyproxy/envoy repository (v1.31.2). The architecture consists of several key components:\\n\\n## Core Listener Manager\\nThe `ListenerManager` interface (envoy/server/listener_manager.h) defines the public API for listener operations. The implementation is in `ListenerManagerImpl` (source/common/listener_manager/listener_manager_impl.h/cc), which is the main orchestrator for:\\n1. **Listener Addition/Removal**: `addOrUpdateListener()` and `removeListener()` methods that handle listener lifecycle\\n2. **Listener Drain Mechanism**: `drainListener()` and `drainFilterChains()` manage graceful listener shutdown through the `DrainingListener` struct that tracks workers pending removal\\n\\n## Listener Configuration\\n`ListenerImpl` (source/common/listener_manager/listener_impl.h/cc) represents individual listener configuration and integrates with `ListenSocketFactoryImpl` which manages socket creation and sharing between workers. The socket factory maintains separate sockets for each worker, handling both reuse_port (individual sockets per worker) and non-reuse_port (shared sockets) modes.\\n\\n## Connection Handler & Worker Thread Assignment\\n`ConnectionHandlerImpl` (source/common/listener_manager/connection_handler_impl.h/cc) is the connection handler that runs on each worker thread and manages the assignment of listeners to worker threads. It maintains a mapping of listener tags to active listeners and handles connection acceptance.\\n\\n`WorkerImpl` (source/server/worker_impl.h/cc) represents a worker thread and receives listener additions from the main thread via `addListener()` method. Each worker has its own event dispatcher and connection handler.\\n\\n## Active Listener Types\\nThe listener manager supports multiple listener implementations:\\n- **TCP Listeners**: `ActiveTcpListener` (source/common/listener_manager/active_tcp_listener.h/cc) extends `OwnedActiveStreamListenerBase`\\n- **UDP Listeners**: `ActiveRawUdpListener` and `ActiveUdpListenerBase` (source/server/active_udp_listener.h/cc)\\n- **QUIC Listeners**: `ActiveQuicListener` and `ActiveQuicListenerFactory` (source/common/quic/active_quic_listener.h/cc)\\n- **Internal Listeners**: `ActiveInternalListener` (source/extensions/bootstrap/internal_listener/active_internal_listener.h/cc)\\n\\nAll these inherit from `ActiveListenerImplBase` (source/server/active_listener_base.h) which provides common listener statistics and lifecycle management.\\n\\n## Stream Listener Base\\n`ActiveStreamListenerBase` (source/common/listener_manager/active_stream_listener_base.h/cc) and its subclass `OwnedActiveStreamListenerBase` provide the foundation for TCP and internal listeners, handling connection acceptance, filter chain management, and connection draining.\\n\\n## Drain Mechanism\\n`DrainManagerImpl` (source/server/drain_manager_impl.h/cc) handles the graceful draining of listeners. When listeners are marked for draining, they track `workers_pending_removal` and drain through a time period before complete removal. The `DrainingFilterChainsManager` (defined in source/common/listener_manager/listener_manager_impl.h) manages individual filter chain draining.\\n\\n## Filter Chain Management\\n`FilterChainManagerImpl` (source/common/listener_manager/filter_chain_manager_impl.h/cc) manages the set of filter chains within a listener and their selection based on connection properties. The `FilterChainFactoryContextCallback` and `ListenerFilterChainFactoryBuilder` (in source/common/listener_manager/listener_manager_impl.h) build filter chains dynamically.\\n\\n## Socket Sharing Between Workers\\nSocket sharing is handled through `ListenSocketFactoryImpl` which pre-creates sockets for all workers during listener creation:\\n- For reuse_port: Creates unique sockets for each worker independently\\n- For non-reuse_port: Creates socket on worker 0 and duplicates for other workers\\nThis ensures socket sharing while allowing each worker to independently close its copy without affecting other workers or the overall listener.\\n\\n## Supporting Components\\n- **LdsApi**: `LdsApiImpl` (source/common/listener_manager/lds_api.h/cc) handles Listener Discovery Service (xDS) updates\\n- **Api Listeners**: `HttpApiListener` and `ApiListenerImplBase` (source/server/api_listener_impl.h/cc) for API-based listeners\\n- **Listener Hooks**: `ListenerHooks` (source/server/listener_hooks.h) provides callbacks for listener lifecycle events\\n- **Validation Listener Manager**: `ValidationListenerManager` (source/extensions/listener_managers/validation_listener_manager/) for configuration validation\\n- **Network Layer**: `TcpListenerImpl` and `UdpListenerImpl` (source/common/network/tcp_listener_impl.h/cc and udp_listener_impl.h/cc) provide the underlying network listener implementations\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":11,"cache_creation_input_tokens":233,"cache_read_input_tokens":98380,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":233},"output_tokens":7,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"83ab92f1-c695-4de9-8436-49af66b1609a","uuid":"a39dda29-b9c4-44c5-9f70-84f9fd4e0dae"}

The implementation is in `ListenerManagerImpl` (source/common/listener_manager/listener_manager_impl.h/cc), which is the main orchestrator for:\\n1. **Listener Addition/Removal**: `addOrUpdateListener()` and `removeListener()` methods that handle listener lifecycle\\n2. **Listener Drain Mechanism**: `drainListener()` and `drainFilterChains()` manage graceful listener shutdown through the `DrainingListener` struct that tracks workers pending removal\\n\\n## Listener Configuration\\n`ListenerImpl` (source/common/listener_manager/listener_impl.h/cc) represents individual listener configuration and integrates with `ListenSocketFactoryImpl` which manages socket creation and sharing between workers. The socket factory maintains separate sockets for each worker, handling both reuse_port (individual sockets per worker) and non-reuse_port (shared sockets) modes.\\n\\n## Connection Handler & Worker Thread Assignment\\n`ConnectionHandlerImpl` (source/common/listener_manager/connection_handler_impl.h/cc) is the connection handler that runs on each worker thread and manages the assignment of listeners to worker threads. It maintains a mapping of listener tags to active listeners and handles connection acceptance.\\n\\n`WorkerImpl` (source/server/worker_impl.h/cc) represents a worker thread and receives listener additions from the main thread via `addListener()` method. Each worker has its own event dispatcher and connection handler.\\n\\n## Active Listener Types\\nThe listener manager supports multiple listener implementations:\\n- **TCP Listeners**: `ActiveTcpListener` (source/common/listener_manager/active_tcp_listener.h/cc) extends `OwnedActiveStreamListenerBase`\\n- **UDP Listeners**: `ActiveRawUdpListener` and `ActiveUdpListenerBase` (source/server/active_udp_listener.h/cc)\\n- **QUIC Listeners**: `ActiveQuicListener` and `ActiveQuicListenerFactory` (source/common/quic/active_quic_listener.h/cc)\\n- **Internal Listeners**: `ActiveInternalListener` (source/extensions/bootstrap/internal_listener/active_internal_listener.h/cc)\\n\\nAll these inherit from `ActiveListenerImplBase` (source/server/active_listener_base.h) which provides common listener statistics and lifecycle management.\\n\\n## Stream Listener Base\\n`ActiveStreamListenerBase` (source/common/listener_manager/active_stream_listener_base.h/cc) and its subclass `OwnedActiveStreamListenerBase` provide the foundation for TCP and internal listeners, handling connection acceptance, filter chain management, and connection draining.\\n\\n## Drain Mechanism\\n`DrainManagerImpl` (source/server/drain_manager_impl.h/cc) handles the graceful draining of listeners. When listeners are marked for draining, they track `workers_pending_removal` and drain through a time period before complete removal. The `DrainingFilterChainsManager` (defined in source/common/listener_manager/listener_manager_impl.h) manages individual filter chain draining.\\n\\n## Filter Chain Management\\n`FilterChainManagerImpl` (source/common/listener_manager/filter_chain_manager_impl.h/cc) manages the set of filter chains within a listener and their selection based on connection properties. The `FilterChainFactoryContextCallback` and `ListenerFilterChainFactoryBuilder` (in source/common/listener_manager/listener_manager_impl.h) build filter chains dynamically.\\n\\n## Socket Sharing Between Workers\\nSocket sharing is handled through `ListenSocketFactoryImpl` which pre-creates sockets for all workers during listener creation:\\n- For reuse_port: Creates unique sockets for each worker independently\\n- For non-reuse_port: Creates socket on worker 0 and duplicates for other workers\\nThis ensures socket sharing while allowing each worker to independently close its copy without affecting other workers or the overall listener.\\n\\n## Supporting Components\\n- **LdsApi**: `LdsApiImpl` (source/common/listener_manager/lds_api.h/cc) handles Listener Discovery Service (xDS) updates\\n- **Api Listeners**: `HttpApiListener` and `ApiListenerImplBase` (source/server/api_listener_impl.h/cc) for API-based listeners\\n- **Listener Hooks**: `ListenerHooks` (source/server/listener_hooks.h) provides callbacks for listener lifecycle events\\n- **Validation Listener Manager**: `ValidationListenerManager` (source/extensions/listener_managers/validation_listener_manager/) for configuration validation\\n- **Network Layer**: `TcpListenerImpl` and `UdpListenerImpl` (source/common/network/tcp_listener_impl.h/cc and udp_listener_impl.h/cc) provide the underlying network listener implementations\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
